## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: solid mechanics (materials science) — thermomechanical constitutive modeling
**Analysis**: The variables are stress (sigma), strain (epsilon), and temperature (T), which is a classic setup for constitutive laws describing elastic/plastic deformation with thermal expansion, temperature-dependent modulus, and thermal softening/hardening.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Isothermal linear elasticity (Hooke-type): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain elastic response at fixed T)
- Linear thermoelasticity with thermal strain: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (thermal expansion shifts the zero-stress strain)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear in T): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (E(T) approximated by a linear function)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (inverse in T): sigma = c0 * epsilon / (c1 + T) (softening captured by decreasing E with T)
- Power-law strain hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (plastic/flow stress scaling with strain)
- Offset power-law (Ludwik/Hollomon variant): sigma = c0 + c1 * (c2 + epsilon)**c3 (accounts for pre-strain/initial hardening offset)
- Voce-type saturating hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(-c2 * epsilon)) (hardening approaches a saturation level)
- Exponential stiffening (Fung-type): sigma = c0 * (exp(c1 * epsilon) - 1) (rapid stiffening at larger strain; common in polymers/biomaterials)
- Logarithmic hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * log(c2 + epsilon) (slowly increasing stress with strain; empirical in some regimes)
- Multiplicative separation of strain and temperature effects: sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * T) (hardening times thermal factor; quick baseline coupled model)
- Thermal softening factor (Johnson–Cook-like, no strain-rate term): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 - (c4 * T)**c5) (flow stress reduced as T rises)
- Thermally activated flow (Eyring/activation-style scaling): sigma = c0 * asinh(c1 * epsilon) * exp(c2 / T) (activation-controlled dependence on T with nonlinear stress–strain)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal expansion effect → use an “effective strain” epsilon - c*(T - T0), so stress can go to zero at nonzero epsilon when T changes.
- Temperature-dependent stiffness/softening → make the coefficient multiplying epsilon decrease with T (e.g., 1/(c+T) or exp(-c*T)) to model reduced modulus at higher temperature.
- Strain hardening behavior → represent sigma increasing faster than linear with epsilon using epsilon**n or exp(c*epsilon).
- Saturating hardening/plastic flow plateau → use (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or tanh(c*epsilon) so incremental hardening decreases with strain.
- Thermal softening near transitions (glass/melt/creep onset) → multiply by a decreasing factor in T such as (c0 - (c1*T)**m) or 1/(1+(c*T)**m).
- Thermally activated deformation mechanisms → include exp(c/T) (or exp(-c/T) depending on sign convention) to capture strong sensitivity to absolute temperature.
- Separable vs coupled thermo-mechanical effects → sigma = f(epsilon)*g(T) suggests independent hardening and thermal scaling; sigma = f(epsilon, T) with mixed terms suggests coupling.
- Low-strain linear regime to nonlinear regime → combine linear term c*epsilon with a nonlinear term (epsilon**n, log(c+epsilon), exp(c*epsilon)-1) to fit elastic-to-plastic transition.
- Ensuring nonnegative stress and smooth yielding → use softplus-like forms log(1 + exp(c*(epsilon-c0))) to emulate a smooth yield onset without discontinuities.

GT (fixed) is the sum of three qualitatively specific parts:
1) **Linear in epsilon with an affine function of T**:  
\[
3.6246\,\epsilon\,( -0.05899\,(T-367.023)+1)=\epsilon\,(aT+b)
\]
so it is exactly **epsilon times (linear-in-T)**.

2) **Arrhenius-in-T term with a non-integer power of epsilon**:  
\[
94.2050\,\epsilon^{0.44749}\exp\!\left(-\frac{55.0161}{8.314\,T}\right)
\]
This is **exp(-const/T)** (not exp(const·T), not exp(const·epsilon)), multiplied by **epsilon^p with p non-integer**.

3) **Gaussian-in-T term multiplied by epsilon**:  
\[
5.12428\,\epsilon\,\exp\!\left(-(T-367.023)^2\right)
\]
This is **exp(-(T-c)^2)** (a Gaussian in T), times epsilon.

So any matching candidate must be able (by choosing its free constants) to simultaneously represent:
- an \(\epsilon(aT+b)\) term,
- a term \(\epsilon^{p}\exp(-k/T)\) with \(p\neq 0,1,2,\dots\),
- a term \(\epsilon\exp(-(T-c)^2)\).
